We recommend you upgrade to the latest available release (2020.2.5) as soon as is practical. For more information, review the Release Notes <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/content/release_notes/orion_platform_2020-2-5_release_notes.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-release-notes-orion-platform-2020-2-5-release-notes-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and KB article <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Remote-Code-Execution-CVE-Frequently-Asked-Questions?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-remote-code-execution-cve-frequently-asked-questions-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p><p class="mb-3">If you have recently upgraded to 2020.2.1 HF2 or 2019.4 HF 6, you are <strong>also protected from SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA</strong>. However, as part of our response to the <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/securityadvisory" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="SUNBURST vulnerability embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-securityadvisory-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">SUNBURST vulnerability</a>, the code-signing certificate used by SolarWinds to sign the affected software versions was revoked <strong>March 8, 2021</strong>, and you may experience performance issues if you do not apply the more recent updates. Please visit our <strong>SolarWinds New Digital Code-Signing Certificate </strong>page at<strong> </strong><a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/new-digital-certificate" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="solarwinds.com/trust-center/new-digital-certificate embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-new-digital-certificate-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">solarwinds.com/trust-center/new-digital-certificate</a> for more information.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Am I safe if I disconnect my Orion server from the internet?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 2</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/6/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Am I safe if I disconnect my Orion server from the internet?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Disconnecting any product from the internet can reduce your attack surface. The Orion Platform is fully functional without an internet connection. Based on our investigations to date, SUNBURST requires an internet connection to be activated and disconnecting your Orion server from the internet should immediately protect your environment from SUNBURST. The vulnerability in the product that allows for the deployment of SUPERNOVA, however, may still be exploited by a malicious actor who accesses your network from inside and not over the internet. Disconnecting from the internet will limit the ability of an external actor exploiting this vulnerability over an internet connection.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>IMPORTANT NOTE:</strong> Disconnecting from the internet is not a recommended substitute for upgrading your Orion software to versions 2019.4.2, 2020.2.4, or 2020.2.5, or applying appropriate patches to older versions if a full upgrade is not possible at this time.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How is SolarWinds addressing SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 3</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/6/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How has SolarWinds addressed SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">We have:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">removed the software builds known to be affected by SUNBURST from our download sites;</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">provided software updates, which include security enhancements, that are designed to address both SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA in supported versions of the Orion server; and</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">provided a fix for customers on unsupported versions further described below.</li></ul><p class="mb-3"><strong>RECOMMENDED ACTIONS</strong>
<br/></p><p class="mb-3">As part of our response to the <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/securityadvisory" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="SUNBURST vulnerability embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-securityadvisory-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">SUNBURST vulnerability</a>, the code-signing certificate used by SolarWinds to sign the affected software versions was revoked <strong>March 8, 2021</strong>. Please visit our <strong>SolarWinds New Digital Code-Signing Certificate </strong>page at<strong> </strong><a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/new-digital-certificate" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="solarwinds.com/trust-center/new-digital-certificate embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-new-digital-certificate-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">solarwinds.com/trust-center/new-digital-certificate</a> for more information.</p><p class="mb-3"> </p><p class="mb-3">We <u>strongly</u> encourage customers to upgrade their Orion products to the latest versions available in the Customer Portal at <a href="https://customerportal.solarwinds.com/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="customerportal.solarwinds.com embed" data-automation-id="-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">customerportal.solarwinds.com</a> that are designed to protect you from SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA. Doing so allows you to the get the full benefit of our updates, improvements, and enhancements.</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you <strong>have</strong> already upgraded to <strong>2020.2.5</strong>, additional security fixes and protections unrelated to SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA are included in this version. For more information, review the Release Notes <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/content/release_notes/orion_platform_2020-2-5_release_notes.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-release-notes-orion-platform-2020-2-5-release-notes-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and KB article <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Remote-Code-Execution-CVE-Frequently-Asked-Questions?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-remote-code-execution-cve-frequently-asked-questions-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you have upgraded to <strong>2020.2.4</strong> or <strong>2019.4 HF 2</strong>, both the SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA vulnerabilities have been addressed in these versions—and they have also been digitally re-signed by newly obtained digital code-signing certificates.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you <strong>have not</strong> already upgraded to <strong>2020.2.5</strong>,<strong> 2020.2.4</strong>, or <strong>2019.4.2</strong>, follow the guidance identified for your current version of your Orion Platform products below to help ensure the security of your environment.</li></ul><p class="mb-3">Here are the steps to take:</p><p class="mb-3">	1. Identify the version of the Orion Platform products you are using by reviewing the directions on how to check that <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Determine-which-version-of-a-SolarWinds-Orion-product-I-have-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-determine-which-version-of-a-solarwinds-orion-product-i-have-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a> or refer to the image below. To check which updates you have applied, please go <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>	From Orion Web Console </strong></p><p class="mb-3">	All product versions are displayed in the footer of the Orion Web Console login page. See the example below of <strong>2019.4 HF 4</strong>:</p><figure style="margin:0"><img alt="SolarWinds footer Orion Web Console login page" loading="lazy" width="712" height="65" decoding="async" class="mb-3">* As a part of the ongoing investigation, we have determined that Orion Platform version 2019.4 unpatched, released in October 2019, contained test modifications to the code base. While this version is not impacted by the SUNBURST vulnerability, it is the first version in which we have seen activity from the attacker at this time. Subsequent releases 2019.4 HF 1, 2019.4 HF 2, 2019.4 HF 3, and 2019.4 HF 4 did not include either test modifications contained in the 2019.4 version or the SUNBURST vulnerability contained in 2019.4 HF 5, 2020.2 unpatched, and 2020.2 HF 1.</p><p class="mb-3">**<strong> </strong>If you apply a SUPERNOVA security patch per the above chart, please visit <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Use-a-script-to-verify-that-the-Supernova-patch-was-applied-to-all-Orion-web-servers?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="this KB article embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-use-a-script-to-verify-that-the-supernova-patch-was-applied-to-all-orion-web-servers-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">this KB article</a> to validate the patch was applied to all Orion Platform web servers. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply the respective patch.<br/></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>*** </strong>If you used the SUPERNOVA Mitigation Script to address the Supernova vulnerability, use the guidance in the document within that package to confirm the temporary patch. Please note that this script has only been tested down to NPM 11.x. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply this script.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>All recommended upgrade</strong> versions are currently available at <a href="https://customerportal.solarwinds.com/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="customerportal.solarwinds.com embed" data-automation-id="-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">customerportal.solarwinds.com</a>. All hotfix updates are cumulative and can be installed from any earlier version. There is no need to install previously released updates.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Based on our investigations to date, we are not aware that the SUNBURST vulnerability affects other versions of our Orion Platform products. Also, while we are still investigating our non-Orion Platform products, we have not seen any evidence that they are impacted by the SUNBURST vulnerability or the SUPERNOVA malware.</strong></p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Are SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA related?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 4</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/26/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Are SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA related?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">While there has been speculation by various sources, based on our investigations to date, we do not have a definitive answer at this time. SolarWinds continues to work closely with federal agencies and third-party cybersecurity firms to determine the answer.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What are SUNSPOT, TEARDROP, and RAINDROP?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 5</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 1/29/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What are SUNSPOT, TEARDROP, and RAINDROP?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">SUNSPOT, TEARDROP, and RAINDROP <strong>are NOT new vulnerabilities</strong> within our products as some reports in the media have indicated, but instead, they are <strong>elements of the SUNBURST attack chain.</strong></p><p class="mb-3">
<br/>SUNSPOT, for example, is the means by which the attackers injected the SUNBURST backdoor during the build process of the Orion Platform, while TEARDROP and RAINDROP are reportedly malware loaders that could be deployed using the SUNBURST backdoor.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How is SolarWinds responding to these security vulnerabilities?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 6</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 1/13/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How is SolarWinds responding to these security vulnerabilities?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">As announced by SolarWinds President and CEO Sudhakar Ramakrishna in his Orange Matter blog, <a href="https://orangematter.solarwinds.com/2021/01/07/our-plan-for-a-safer-solarwinds-and-customer-community/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="Our Plan for a Safer SolarWinds and Customer Community embed" data-automation-id="2021-01-07-our-plan-for-a-safer-solarwinds-and-customer-community-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2"><em>Our Plan for a Safer SolarWinds and Customer Community</em></a>, we are taking key steps to ensure the security and integrity of the software that we deliver to customers.</p><p class="mb-3">All new hotfixes and patches we have released since SUNBURST was detected have undergone these new levels of scrutiny. SolarWinds is increasing existing actions and taking additional actions across the enterprise to further harden and improve the security of our environment and products:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Increased hardening of build environment and build pipeline</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Auditing and surveillance</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Environmental reviews by third-party cybersecurity experts</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Release code penetration testing (pentesting)</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Increased scanning of downloadable bits</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Scanning and analysis of source code and build output</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Refreshing of all employee and contractor credentials and credential security and elevating access restriction</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Re-signing of all release code with new certificates</li></ul><p class="mb-3">In addition, we’re elevating our ongoing architectural focus on continually improving the way we design, build, and support our products.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What actions should I take?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 7</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/6/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What actions should I take?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">As part of our response to the <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/securityadvisory" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="SUNBURST vulnerability embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-securityadvisory-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">SUNBURST vulnerability</a>, the code-signing certificate used by SolarWinds to sign the affected software versions was revoked <strong>March 8, 2021</strong>. Please visit our <strong>SolarWinds New Digital Code-Signing Certificate </strong>page at<strong> </strong><a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/new-digital-certificate" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="solarwinds.com/trust-center/new-digital-certificate embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-new-digital-certificate-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">solarwinds.com/trust-center/new-digital-certificate</a> for more information.</p><p class="mb-3">We encourage all customers to run only supported versions of our products and to upgrade to the latest versions to the get the full benefit of our updates, improvements and enhancements. The latest versions of our products are available in the Customer Portal at <a href="https://customerportal.solarwinds.com/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="customerportal.solarwinds.com embed" data-automation-id="-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">customerportal.solarwinds.com</a>. Based on our investigation, we recommend that all customers of Orion Platform products apply the latest updates applicable to the version of the product they have deployed.</p><p class="mb-3">To take advantage of our latest available security updates protections for the products you have deployed, we recommend all active maintenance customers of Orion Platform products <strong>upgrade to version 2020.2.5</strong> as soon as possible. For more information, review the Release Notes <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/content/release_notes/orion_platform_2020-2-5_release_notes.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-release-notes-orion-platform-2020-2-5-release-notes-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and KB article <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Remote-Code-Execution-CVE-Frequently-Asked-Questions?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-remote-code-execution-cve-frequently-asked-questions-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p><p class="mb-3">Orion Platform versions 2019.4.2 and 2020.2.4 were designed to protect you from both the SUNBURST vulnerability and the SUPERNOVA malware and have been re-signed with our newly obtained digital-signing certificate.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>You may need to synchronize your license prior to applying the hotfix. </strong>Please follow the steps <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/success_center/orionplatform/Content/Core-Centralized-Licensing-Synchronize.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here ebed" License Offline” section from <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/Content/Core-Centralized-Licensing-Activate-Licenses.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" you’re unable to upgrade at this time, we have provided a script that customers can install to temporarily protect their environment against SUPERNOVA. The script is available at <a href="https://downloads.solarwinds.com/solarwinds/Support/SupernovaMitigation.zip" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="https://downloads.solarwinds.com/solarwinds/Support/SupernovaMitigation.zip embed" data-automation-id="solarwinds-support-supernovamitigation-zip-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">https://downloads.solarwinds.com/solarwinds/Support/SupernovaMitigation.zip</a>. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply this script.</p><p class="mb-3">We also recommend customers review our <strong>Secure Configuration for the Orion Platform</strong> guide <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/content/core-secure-configuration.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-core-secure-configuration-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a> for additional best practices.</p><br/></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How do I know what version I’m on?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 8</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How do I know what version I’m on?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">If you aren’t sure which version of the Orion Platform products you’re using, you can see directions on how to check that <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Determine-which-version-of-a-SolarWinds-Orion-product-I-have-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-determine-which-version-of-a-solarwinds-orion-product-i-have-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>. To check which hotfix updates you’ve applied, please go <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" target="_self" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How do I know if my environment was exposed?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 9</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/24/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How do I know if my environment was exposed?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">To get started, please review the <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/securityadvisory" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="Security Advisory page embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-securityadvisory-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">Security Advisory page</a> on our website, as we update it with the latest information. Next, determine if your environment is at risk by verifying the version of the Orion Platform you have installed <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Determine-which-version-of-a-SolarWinds-Orion-product-I-have-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-determine-which-version-of-a-solarwinds-orion-product-i-have-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and verify which hotfix updates you have installed <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p><p class="mb-3">Once you’ve determined which version you have installed, go to the <strong>QUESTION 19</strong> to see what steps you should take.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How do I upgrade my Orion Platform version?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 10</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/18/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How do I upgrade my Orion Platform version?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Please check <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/success_center/orionplatform/content/orion_platform_installation_guide.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="this article embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-orion-platform-installation-guide-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">this article</a> to learn more about upgrading your version of the Orion Platform software.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">My antivirus software is alerting on the of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll – am I infected?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 11</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/16/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>My antivirus software is alerting on the of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll – am I infected?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">We’ve been advised some Endpoint Security tools are alerting on<strong> all</strong> versions of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll, including versions that we do not believe were impacted by SUNBURST. We’re working with those vendors to update their security definitions to eliminate these false positives.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Some endpoint security tools flag old Orion installers left behind after upgrading to protected versions. Do these alerts mean that I am still at risk?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 12</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/5/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Some endpoint security tools flag old Orion installers left behind after upgrading to protected versions. Do these alerts mean that I am still at risk?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Not necessarily. We do not have evidence to suggest that the mere presence of these old Orion installers puts you at risk.</p><p class="mb-3">If you’ve already upgraded to 2019.4.2, 2020.2.4, or 2020.2.5, the affected SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll was removed and replaced from the runtime area, prohibiting it from executing further. However, depending on the path taken to upgrade, some old versions of the .dll or MSIs were not fully removed.</p><p class="mb-3">To eliminate these alerts, we recommend that you remove those old installer files by following the steps outlined <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Anti-Virus-Still-Detecting-Affected-SolarWinds-Orion-Core-BusinessLayer-dll-after-Upgrade?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-anti-virus-still-detecting-affected-solarwinds-orion-core-businesslayer-dll-after-upgrade-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Has the Department of Homeland Security issued an Emergency Directive on this vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 13</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/6/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Has the Department of Homeland Security issued an Emergency Directive on this vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Yes, the Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA) Computer Emergency Readiness Team (CERT), part of the Department of Homeland Security (DHS), CERT issued <a href="https://cyber.dhs.gov/ed/21-01/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="Emergency Directive 21-01 embed" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-automation-id="ed-21-01-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">Emergency Directive 21-01</a> on December 13, 2020 regarding this issue. CERT issued <a href="https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa20-352a" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="Alert (AA20-352A) embed" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-automation-id="ncas-alerts-aa20-352a-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">Alert (AA20-352A</a>), titled <em>Advanced Persistent Threat Compromise of Government Agencies, Critical Infrastructure, and Private Sector Organizations</em>, as an update to ED 21-01 on December 17, 2020, based on our coordination with the agency. DHS released Supplemental Guidance to ED 21-01 on December 18, 2020, CERT revised its Alert AA20-352A on December 19, 2020, DHS released Supplemental Guidance v2 on December 30, 2020, and released Supplemental Guidance v3 on January 6, 2021 as part of our ongoing coordination with the agency. Additionally, CISA released a malware analysis report of SUPERNOVA on January 27, 2021.</p><p class="mb-3">The latest information can be found on the<strong> CISA Supply Chain Compromise</strong> page at <a href="https://www.cisa.gov/supply-chain-compromise" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="https://www.cisa.gov/supply-chain-compromise embed" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-automation-id="supply-chain-compromise-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">https://www.cisa.gov/supply-chain-compromise</a>.</p><p class="mb-3">The latest release, Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.5</strong> is now available in the SolarWinds Customer Portal at <a href="https://customerportal.solarwinds.com/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="customerportal.solarwinds.com embed" data-automation-id="-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">customerportal.solarwinds.com</a>, in accordance with ED 21-01.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Why does CISA recommend users split out the web server from the Orion Application server?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 14</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 2/2/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Why does CISA recommend users split out the web server from the Orion Application server?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">By splitting out the web server from the application server, you can leverage different controls to further secure your deployment. Orion Platform users need access to the web server (port 443), which could have a large surface area, and the web server does <em>not</em> need to have network access to the monitored devices – only the pollers (including the main poller) need network access. By deploying a separate web server and shutting down and/or blocking access to the web console on the main poller, you can put a firebreak between the web interface used by users and the monitored systems.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What is SolarWinds doing to help find a solution?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 15</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 1/13/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What is SolarWinds doing to help find a solution?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Since the cyberattack on our customers and SolarWinds, we&#x27;ve worked around the clock to support our customers. As we shared in our <a href="https://orangematter.solarwinds.com/2021/01/07/our-plan-for-a-safer-solarwinds-and-customer-community/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="recent update embed" data-automation-id="2021-01-07-our-plan-for-a-safer-solarwinds-and-customer-community-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">recent update</a>, we&#x27;re partnering with multiple industry-leading cybersecurity experts to strengthen our systems, further enhance our product development processes, and adapt the ways that we deliver powerful, affordable, and secure solutions to our customers. Read more on the latest findings from our investigation of SUNBURST <a href="https://orangematter.solarwinds.com/2021/01/11/new-findings-from-our-investigation-of-sunburst/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="2021-01-11-new-findings-from-our-investigation-of-sunburst-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p><p class="mb-3">We have retained third-party cybersecurity experts to assist in an investigation of these matters, including whether a vulnerability in the Orion Platform products was exploited as a point of any infiltration of customer systems, and in the development of appropriate mitigation and remediation plans. SolarWinds is cooperating and sharing information with partners, vendors, law enforcement, and the intelligence and government agencies around the world to assist in investigations related to this incident.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>We are solely focused on our customers and the industry we serve.</strong> Our top priority has been to take all steps necessary to ensure that our and our customers’ environments are secure. We are taking extraordinary measures to accomplish this goal. We shared all of our proprietary code libraries that we believed to have been affected by SUNBURST to give security professionals the information they needed to do their research. We also have had numerous conversations with security professionals to further assist them in their research. We were very pleased and proud to hear that colleagues in the industry discovered a “killswitch” that will prevent the malicious code from being used to create a compromise.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What if I can’t upgrade right now? How do I ensure the security of my Orion server?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 16</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/26/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What if I can’t upgrade right now? How do I ensure the security of my Orion server?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">If you can’t upgrade immediately, please follow the guidelines available <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/content/core-secure-configuration.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-core-secure-configuration-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a> for improving the security of your Orion Platform instance. Primary mitigation steps include:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Ensure the Orion Platform is installed behind a firewall,</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Disable internet access for the Orion Platform, and</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Limit the ports and connections to only what is required to operate your platform.</li></ul><p class="mb-3">If you’re unable to upgrade at this time, we have provided a script that customers can install to temporarily protect their environment against SUPERNOVA. The script is available at <a href="https://downloads.solarwinds.com/solarwinds/Support/SupernovaMitigation.zip" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="https://downloads.solarwinds.com/solarwinds/Support/SupernovaMitigation.zip embed" data-automation-id="solarwinds-support-supernovamitigation-zip-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">https://downloads.solarwinds.com/solarwinds/Support/SupernovaMitigation.zip</a>. Please note that this script has only been tested down to NPM 11.x. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply this script.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">I have downloaded a file from my Customer Portal and want to verify it is legitimate. How can I do that?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 17</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/18/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>I have downloaded a file from my Customer Portal and want to verify it is legitimate. How can I do that?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">A list of SolarWinds Checksums is available <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/product-checksum" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="product-checksum-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a> for your reference. If you’re unaware of how to perform this validation, one such method is using “Get-FileHash” from the Microsoft PowerShell Utility documented <a href="https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/powershell/module/microsoft.powershell.utility/get-filehash?view=powershell-7.1" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" target="_blank" class="mb-3"><strong>*</strong>As a part of the ongoing investigation, we have determined that Orion Platform version 2019.4 <u>unpatched</u>, released in October 2019, contained test modifications to the code base. While this version is not impacted by the SUNBURST vulnerability, it is the first version in which we have seen activity from the attacker at this time. Subsequent releases 2019.4 HF 1, 2019.4 HF 2, 2019.4 HF 3, and 2019.4 HF 4 did not include either test modifications contained in the 2019.4 version or the SUNBURST vulnerability contained in 2019.4 HF 5, 2020.2 with no hotfix and 2020.2 HF 1.</p><p class="mb-3">** If you apply a SUPERNOVA security patch per the above chart, please visit <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Use-a-script-to-verify-that-the-Supernova-patch-was-applied-to-all-Orion-web-servers?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="this KB article embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-use-a-script-to-verify-that-the-supernova-patch-was-applied-to-all-orion-web-servers-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">this KB article</a> to validate the patch was applied to all Orion Platform web servers. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply the respective patch.</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>*** </strong>If you use the SUPERNOVA Mitigation Script to address the Supernova vulnerability, use the guidance in the document within that package to confirm the temporary patch. Please note that this script has only been tested down to NPM 11.x. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply this script.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">If your environment was compromised, why is it safe for us to install these updates/trust your code? OR What are you doing to prevent future incidents moving forward?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong><span id="question19">QUESTION 19</span></strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 1/13/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>If your environment was compromised, why is it safe for us to install these updates/trust your code? OR What are you doing to prevent future incidents moving forward?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Our investigations are ongoing, but since the vulnerabilities related to SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA were discovered, we have reviewed our environment, giving an initial focus on ensuring the security of our build environment, including our source code repositories. We have reviewed the architecture of the build environment, the privileged and non-privileged users that have access to the build environment, and the network surrounding the build environment.</p><p class="mb-3">We have retained third-party cybersecurity experts to assist in an investigation of these matters, including whether the vulnerabilities were exploited as a point of any infiltration of any customer systems, and in the development of appropriate mitigation and remediation plans to help ensure future releases are protected. We are also cooperating and sharing information with our partners, vendors, and law enforcement, intelligence, and government agencies around the world to assist in investigations and to avoid vulnerabilities in future releases.</p><p class="mb-3">Our investigations are ongoing, and we will continue to focus on ensuring that our environments are secure and protected. Read more about our investigation <a href="https://orangematter.solarwinds.com/2021/01/11/new-findings-from-our-investigation-of-sunburst/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="2021-01-11-new-findings-from-our-investigation-of-sunburst-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and read more about the actions we&#x27;re taking moving forward <a href="https://orangematter.solarwinds.com/2021/01/07/our-plan-for-a-safer-solarwinds-and-customer-community/" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" target="_self" data-automation-id="2021-01-07-our-plan-for-a-safer-solarwinds-and-customer-community-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">I still have more questions about this issue and my environment’s security—who can I talk to?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 20</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>I still have more questions about this issue and my environment’s security—who can I talk to?</strong></p>We are making regular updates to our Security Advisory page at <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/securityadvisory" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="solarwinds.com/securityadvisory embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-securityadvisory-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">solarwinds.com/securityadvisory</a>.</div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Why can’t you tell us more about what’s going on?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 21</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Why can’t you tell us more about what’s going on?</strong></p>While we understand there may a lot of questions on this situation, we will continue to communicate information as it’s available. Our investigations into these matters are ongoing, and we continue to work closely with law enforcement, intelligence and other government agencies around the world to investigate them. We are also working with leading security experts in these investigations and to help further secure our products and internal systems.<br/></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What about the vulnerabilities disclosed by Trustwave?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 22</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 2/5/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What about the vulnerabilities disclosed by Trustwave?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">First, it’s important to note these vulnerabilities are not related to the SUNBURST attack, or to SUPERNOVA.</p><p class="mb-3">Vulnerabilities of varying degrees are common in all software products, including recent patches for Apple and Microsoft that solve critical vulnerabilities, but we understand there is heightened scrutiny on SolarWinds right now. SolarWinds has always been committed to working with our customers and other organizations to identify and remediate any vulnerabilities across our product portfolio in a responsible way. Trustwave is a leading threat detection company that responsibly reports product vulnerabilities to companies as they are discovered prior to broader announcement to allow companies to develop remediations to protect their customers.</p><p class="mb-3">The vulnerabilities announced by Trustwave concerning the Orion® Platform were addressed in Orion Platform version 2020.2.4, released January 25, 2021. The vulnerabilities concerning Serv-U were addressed in Serv-U version 15.2.2 HF1, released January 22, 2021. To review the list of currently supported versions of these products, please review the <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Currently-supported-software-versions?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="documentation embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-currently-supported-software-versions-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">documentation</a>.</p><p class="mb-3">Trustwave identified three vulnerabilities, two in the Orion Platform and one in our Serv-U file transfer product. To our knowledge, none of these vulnerabilities have been exploited. The three vulnerabilities could be described as follows:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">The first, which affects the Orion Platform, allows for an unprivileged user to extract passwords from the SQL Server database.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">The second allows a remote user to execute a command against the Microsoft Message Queue service used by the Orion Platform.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">The third allows an attacker to gain access to the Serv-U FTP server by creating an unauthorized user account.</li></ul></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What about the issue disclosed by Sophos?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 23</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 2/5/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What about the issue disclosed by Sophos?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">In the case of the Sophos announcement, it is important to note this is <strong>NOT</strong> a reported vulnerability in the Orion Platform product. This situation was the result of a compromise within an individual company&#x27;s network unrelated to SolarWinds. That breach enabled attackers to add malicious code to the Orion Platform software instance within the customer&#x27;s network.</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">In November of 2020, Sophos investigated an environment infected with a Ragnar Locker attack in which hundreds of computers were compromised.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">One of the computers compromised in the Ragnar Locker attack was a Windows server hosting the Orion product.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">The threat actor had full administrative access to the Windows server and was able to copy and replace a signed .dll shipped with the Orion Platform software with an unsigned, compromised version.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">This compromised code was not shipped with the Orion Platform software.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Following the Orion Secure Configuration Guide mitigates the risk of this type of attack.</li></ul></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What is SUPERNOVA?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 24</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 1/29/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What is SUPERNOVA?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Shortly after SUNBURST was announced, third parties and the media publicly reported on a malware, now referred to as SUPERNOVA. Based on our investigation, this malware could be deployed through an exploitation of a vulnerability in the Orion Platform. Like other software companies, we seek to responsibly disclose vulnerabilities in our products to our customers while also mitigating the risk that bad actors seek to exploit those vulnerabilities by releasing updates to our products before we disclose the vulnerabilities.</p><p class="mb-3">CISA released a <a href="https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/analysis-reports/ar21-027a" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="malware analysis report embed" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-automation-id="ncas-analysis-reports-ar21-027a-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">malware analysis report</a> on SUPERNOVA on January 27, 2021. The SUPERNOVA malware consisted of two components. The first was a malicious, unsigned webshell .dll “app_web_logoimagehandler.ashx.b6031896.dll” specifically written to be used on the Orion Platform. The second is the exploitation of a vulnerability in the Orion Platform to enable deployment of the malicious code. The latest updates were designed to remediate this vulnerability in all supported versions of the Orion Platform.</p><p class="mb-3">We constantly work to enhance the security of our products and to protect our customers and ourselves because hackers and other cybercriminals are always seeking new ways to find and attack their victims. We work closely with our customers to address and remediate any potential concerns, and we encourage all customers to run only supported versions of our products and to upgrade to the latest versions to the get the full benefit of our updates, improvements, and enhancements.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Is SUPERNOVA another supply chain attack?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 25</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/26/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Is SUPERNOVA another supply chain attack?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Based on our investigation to date, SUPERNOVA is not malicious code embedded within the builds of our Orion<sup>®</sup> Platform as a supply chain attack. It is malware that is separately placed on a server that requires unauthorized access to a customer’s network and is designed to appear to be part of a SolarWinds product.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What indicators of compromise (IOCs) of the SUPERNOVA malware have you identified?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 26</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/29/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What indicators of compromise (IOCs) of the SUPERNOVA malware have you identified?</strong></p>Through our investigations, our retention of a third-party cybersecurity firm, and in cooperation with the law enforcement, intelligence and other government agencies around the world in investigations related to the SUPERNOVA vulnerability, we’ve identified the following IOC:<p class="mb-3">-The SUPERNOVA malware [app_web_logoimagehandler.ashx.b6031896.dll] with the file hash:</p><p class="mb-3">-sha256 of the file app_web_logoimagehandler.ashx.b6031896.dll is:
<br/>c15abaf51e78ca56c0376522d699c978217bf041a3bd3c71d09193efa5717c71</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How can I confirm if I’ve applied either the SUPERNOVA mitigation script or one of the SUPERNOVA security fixes to my Orion server(s)?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 27</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/31/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How can I confirm if I’ve applied either the SUPERNOVA mitigation script or one of the SUPERNOVA security fixes to my Orion server(s)?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">If you’re running Orion Platform version 2018.2, 2018.4, or 2019.2, you can run the script available <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Use-a-script-to-verify-that-the-Supernova-patch-was-applied-to-all-Orion-web-servers?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-use-a-script-to-verify-that-the-supernova-patch-was-applied-to-all-orion-web-servers-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a> to verify one of the SUPERNOVA Security Fixes (2018.2 HF6 Security Fix, 2018.4 HF3 Security Fix, 2019.2 HF3 Security Fix) for the recent SUPERNOVA <a href="https://www.solarwinds.com/sa-overview/securityadvisory" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="security vulnerability embed" data-automation-id="sa-overview-securityadvisory-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">security vulnerability</a> has been applied to your main Orion server and any additional web servers. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply the respective patch.</p><p class="mb-3">If you used the SUPERNOVA Mitigation Script to address the Supernova vulnerability, use the guidance in the document within that package to confirm the temporary patch. If you reinstall your Orion server, you will need to reapply this script.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What is SUNBURST?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 28</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/18/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What is SUNBURST?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">SolarWinds was the victim of a cyberattack that inserted a vulnerability (SUNBURST) within our Orion® Platform software builds for versions <strong>2019.4 HF 5</strong>, <strong>2020.2 </strong><u><strong>unpatched</strong></u>, and <strong>2020.2 HF 1</strong>, which, if present and activated, could potentially allow an attacker to compromise the server on which the Orion Platform products run. SUNBURST was very sophisticated supply chain attack, which refers to a disruption in a standard process resulting in a compromised result with a goal of being able to attack subsequent users of the software.</p><p class="mb-3">Based on our investigation, it appears that the code was intended to be used in a targeted way as its exploitation requires manual intervention. We’ve been advised that the sophistication and nature of SUNBURST indicates that it may have been conducted by an outside nation state, but SolarWinds has not verified the identity of the attacker.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How extensive is the impact of SUNBURST?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 29</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/18/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How extensive is the impact of SUNBURST?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Based on our investigations to date, which are ongoing, we believe that the SUNBURST vulnerability was inserted within the Orion Platform products and existed in updates released between March and June 2020 (which we call the “relevant period”) as a result of a compromise of the Orion software build system and was not present in the source code repository of the Orion Platform products. SolarWinds has taken steps to remediate the compromise of the Orion software build system and we’re investigating what additional steps, if any, should be taken. <strong>Also, while we are still investigating our non-Orion products, we have not seen any evidence that they are impacted by SUNBURST. </strong>Based on our investigations to date, SolarWinds currently believes that:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Orion Platform products downloaded, implemented or updated during the relevant period contained the SUNBURST vulnerability;</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Orion Platform products downloaded and implemented <strong>before</strong> the relevant period and not updated during the relevant period did not contain the SUNBURST vulnerability;</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Orion Platform products downloaded and implemented <strong>after </strong>the relevant period did not contain the SUNBURST vulnerability; and</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Previously affected versions of the Orion Platform products that were updated with a build released <strong>after </strong>the relevant period no longer contained the SUNBURST vulnerability; however, the server on which the affected Orion Platform products ran may have been compromised during the period in which the SUNBURST vulnerability existed.</li></ul></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What should I do if I believe my environment has been compromised by the SUNBURST vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 30</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/6/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What should I do if I believe my environment has been compromised by the SUNBURST vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">If you believe your environment has been compromised by the SUNBURST vulnerability, below are the recommended steps to take:</p><p class="mb-3">First, determine the version of the Orion® Platform products you have installed <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Determine-which-version-of-a-SolarWinds-Orion-product-I-have-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-determine-which-version-of-a-solarwinds-orion-product-i-have-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and verify which hotfix updates you have installed <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-verify-hotfixes-that-have-been-installed-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you <strong>have</strong> already upgraded to <strong>2020.2.5</strong>, additional security fixes and protections unrelated to SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA are included in this version. For more information, review the Release Notes <a href="https://documentation.solarwinds.com/en/Success_Center/orionplatform/content/release_notes/orion_platform_2020-2-5_release_notes.htm" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="en-success-center-orionplatform-content-release-notes-orion-platform-2020-2-5-release-notes-htm-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>, and KB article <a href="https://support.solarwinds.com/SuccessCenter/s/article/Remote-Code-Execution-CVE-Frequently-Asked-Questions?language=en_US" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="here embed" data-automation-id="successcenter-s-article-remote-code-execution-cve-frequently-asked-questions-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">here</a>.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you have upgraded to <strong>2020.2.4</strong> or <strong>2019.4 HF 2</strong>, both the SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA vulnerabilities have been addressed in these versions—and they have also been digitally re-signed by newly obtained digital code-signing certificates.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you <strong>have not</strong> already upgraded to <strong>2020.2.5</strong>,<strong> 2020.2.4</strong>, or <strong>2019.4.2</strong>, follow the guidance identified for your current version of your Orion Platform products below to help ensure the security of your environment:</li><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you’re currently running Orion Platform version <strong>2019.4 HF 4</strong>, we recommend you upgrade to <strong>2020.2.5</strong>, or <strong>2019.4.2</strong> if you are unable to upgrade to the latest version at this time.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you’re currently running Orion Platform version <strong>2019.4 HF 5</strong>, we recommend you rebuild your Orion server/VM for all pollers and install Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.5</strong> or <strong>2019.4.2</strong> if you are unable to upgrade to the latest version at this time.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you’re currently running Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.1</strong>, <strong>but have run any of the previous infected versions</strong>, rebuild your Orion server and/or VM for all pollers and install Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.5</strong> on a fresh machine.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you are running a version prior to Orion Platform version<strong> 2019.4 HF 4</strong>, we do not believe that your system was compromised with this vulnerability. We still recommend as a best practice that you upgrade to the latest version, Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.5</strong>, to take advantage of the latest security improvements.</li></ul></ul><p class="mb-3">To help protect your system, you should also block DNS access to any of the following:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">avsvmcloud[.]com</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">panhardware[.]com</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">databasegalore[.]com</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">freescanonline[.]com</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">thedoccloud[.]com</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">deftsecurity[.]com</li></ul><p class="mb-3">
<br/>If you have the expertise to take the additional following action items, please do so:</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Forensically image system memory and/or host operating systems hosting all instances of SolarWinds Orion Platform [versions <strong>2019.4 HF 5</strong>, <strong>2020.2</strong> <strong>unpatched</strong>, and <strong>2020.2 HF 1</strong>].</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Analyze stored network traffic for indications of compromise, including new external DNS domains.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">Consult with any security vendors with whom you currently have a relationship on their recommendations.</li></ul></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">If my Orion server currently or previously had a SUNBURST vulnerable version, should I simply upgrade or should I rebuild my Orion server? What about my database?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 31</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 4/6/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>If my Orion server currently or previously had a SUNBURST vulnerable version, should I simply upgrade or should I rebuild my Orion server? What about my database?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">We encourage all customers to run only supported versions of our products and to upgrade to the latest versions to the get the full benefit of our updates, improvements and enhancements.</p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you <strong>never ran</strong> a known, affected version on your Orion server, <strong>we do not recommend that you rebuild</strong>. We still recommend as a best practice that you upgrade to the latest version, Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.5</strong>,<strong> </strong>to take advantage of the latest security improvements.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you ran a known, affected version of your Orion server <u><strong>and</strong></u> it had access to the internet, we recommend that <strong>you rebuild the server</strong>.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If your Orion server had no access to the internet, <strong>we do not recommend that you rebuild</strong>. An upgrade to Orion Platform version <strong>2020.2.5 </strong>will be sufficient.</li></ul><p class="mb-3">If you rebuild your servers, here are the factors to consider in deciding whether to retain your Orion Database:</p><p class="mb-3"></p><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3"><strong>Reference the </strong><a href="https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa20-352a" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="CISA Alert (AA20-352A) embed" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-automation-id="ncas-alerts-aa20-352a-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2"><strong>CISA Alert (AA20-352A)</strong></a>:</li><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you fall into <strong>Category 2</strong>, you should be able to re-install the software and retain your Orion databases for the platform, for flow, and for logs—consistent with a thorough risk evaluation.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you fall into <strong>Category 3</strong>, your Orion installation—including the Orion databases—are equally as vulnerable as the rest of the environment, and you should follow your incident response procedures.</li></ul><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3"><strong>Additional considerations:</strong></li><ul class="list-inside list-disc pl-10"><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">We are not aware of any indications at this time that the SUNBURST vulnerability routinely altered the Orion databases in any way.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">You may want to audit configurations stored in the database, like alert actions, or executable scripts to confirm they have not been tampered with.</li><li class="-indent-6 marker:text-swdc-orange-400 last:mb-3">If you chose to rebuild your databases, follow your incident response procedures to image and retain your databases, particularly your flow database for forensic analysis.</li></ul></ul></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">I want to manually check my version of the SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll for the SUNBURST vulnerability. Do you know a way to do that?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 32</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/16/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>I want to manually check my version of the SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll for the SUNBURST vulnerability. Do you know a way to do that?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">You should check your Orion server, any additional polling engine, high availability (HA) engines, and additional web servers. You can use the following file hash information to check whether you have the version with the inserted vulnerability:</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>From Windows, open PowerShell and run the following (adjusting the file path if a different installation path was used):</strong></p><p class="mb-3">	Get-FileHash &quot;C:\Program Files (x86)\SolarWinds\Orion\SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll&quot;</p><p class="mb-3"><strong><em>Versions not known to contain the SUNBURST vulnerability:</em></strong></p><p class="mb-3">	2020.2.1 RTM sha256sum of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll (file version 2020.2.15300.12766)</p><p class="mb-3">	143632672dcb6ef324343739636b984f5c52ece0e078cfee7c6cac4a3545403a</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>	(No hotfix applied, not the known compromised version)</strong></p><p class="mb-3">	2020.2.1 HF 1 sha256sum of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll (file version 2020.2.15300.12766)</p><p class="mb-3">	143632672dcb6ef324343739636b984f5c52ece0e078cfee7c6cac4a3545403a</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>	(Not the known compromised version; NOTE: same as 2020.2.1 RTM – this hotfix does not update that DLL)</strong></p><p class="mb-3">	2019.4 HF6 - file version 2019.4.5200.9106 - sha256 8DFE613B00D495FB8905BDF6E1317D3E3AC1F63A626032FA2BDAD4750887EE8A</p><p class="mb-3">
<br/>	2020.2.1 HF2 - file version 2020.2.15300.12901 - sha256 CC870C07EEB672AB33B6C2BE51B173AD5564AF5D98BFC02DA02367A9E349A76F</p><p class="mb-3"><strong><em>Versions known to contain the SUNBURST vulnerability:</em></strong></p><p class="mb-3">	sha256 of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll from 2019.4 HF 5: 32519b85c0b422e4656de6e6c41878e95fd95026267daab4215ee59c107d6c77</p><p class="mb-3">
<br/>	sha256 of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll from 2020.2: ce77d116a074dab7a22a0fd4f2c1ab475f16eec42e1ded3c0b0aa8211fe858d6</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>	Hashes from fixes provided to individual customers, sometimes called “Buddy Drops”</strong></p><p class="mb-3">	019085a76ba7126fff22770d71bd901c325fc68ac55aa743327984e89f4b0134 </p><p
