class="mb-3"> </p><p class="mb-3"><strong>NOTE:</strong> If you’re checking files using MacOS or Linux, the standard “sha256sum” tool can be used.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What indicators of compromise (IOCs) of the SUNBURST vulnerability have you identified?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 33</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What indicators of compromise (IOCs) of the SUNBURST vulnerability have you identified?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Through our investigations, our retention of a third-party cybersecurity firm, and in cooperation with the law enforcement, intelligence, and other government agencies around the world in investigations related to the SUNBURST vulnerability, we’ve identified the following IOCs</p><p class="mb-3">-[SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll] with one of the file hashes listed below:</p><p class="mb-3">-sha256 of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll from 2019.4 HF 5: 32519b85c0b422e4656de6e6c41878e95fd95026267daab4215ee59c107d6c77</p><p class="mb-3">-sha256 of SolarWinds.Orion.Core.BusinessLayer.dll from 2020.2: ce77d116a074dab7a22a0fd4f2c1ab475f16eec42e1ded3c0b0aa8211fe858d6</p><p class="mb-3"></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Additional Hashes from Hotfix and Buddy drop releases</strong></p><p class="mb-3">-019085a76ba7126fff22770d71bd901c325fc68ac55aa743327984e89f4b0134</p><p class="mb-3">-ac1b2b89e60707a20e9eb1ca480bc3410ead40643b386d624c5d21b47c02917c</p><p class="mb-3">-c09040d35630d75dfef0f804f320f8b3d16a481071076918e9b236a321c1ea77</p><p class="mb-3">-dab758bf98d9b36fa057a66cd0284737abf89857b73ca89280267ee7caf62f3b</p><p class="mb-3">-eb6fab5a2964c5817fb239a7a5079cabca0a00464fb3e07155f28b0a57a2c0ed</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How do I know someone didn&#x27;t exploit the SUNBURST vulnerability and move horizontally in my environment and compromise another system?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 34</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/20/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How do I know someone didn&#x27;t exploit the SUNBURST vulnerability and move horizontally in my environment and compromise another system?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">If the SUNBURST vulnerability was exploited in your environment, you may see network traffic from the Orion server to the internet. This traffic would be directed to a domain other than SolarWinds domain. Horizontal or lateral movement by an attacker would indicate that they have gained privileged level access to your environment. Increased security event monitoring, close inspection of server and application access logs, and understanding what local accounts exist on your corporate systems will help to identify any signs of misuse.</p><p class="mb-3">For further details, please see <strong>CERT Alert (AA20-352A), Advanced Persistent Threat Compromise of Government Agencies, Critical Infrastructure, and Private Sector Organizations</strong>, updated December 19, 2020: <a href="https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa20-352a" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa20-352a embed" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-automation-id="ncas-alerts-aa20-352a-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa20-352a</a>.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What products are affected by the SUNBURST vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 35</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/24/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What products are affected by the SUNBURST vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">We have identified the following products as being affected: Orion Platform versions <strong>2019.4 HF 5</strong>, <strong>2020.2 </strong><u><strong>unpatched</strong></u><strong>, </strong>and<strong> 2020.2 HF 1</strong>, including:</p><p class="mb-3">	Application Centric Monitor (ACM)
<br/>	Database Performance Analyzer <strong>Integration Module*</strong> (DPAIM*)
<br/>	Enterprise Operations Console (EOC)
<br/>	High Availability (HA)
<br/>	IP Address Manager (IPAM)
<br/>	Log Analyzer (LA)
<br/>	Network Automation Manager (NAM)
<br/>	Network Configuration Manager (NCM)
<br/>	Network Operations Manager (NOM)
<br/>	Network Performance Monitor (NPM)
<br/>	NetFlow Traffic Analyzer (NTA)
<br/>	Server &amp; Application Monitor (SAM)
<br/>	Server Configuration Monitor (SCM)
<br/>	Storage Resource Monitor (SRM)
<br/>	User Device Tracker (UDT)
<br/>	Virtualization Manager (VMAN)
<br/>	VoIP &amp; Network Quality Manager (VNQM)
<br/>	Web Performance Monitor (WPM)</p><p class="mb-3"><strong>	*NOTE: </strong>Please note DPAIM is an integration module and <strong>is not the same</strong> as Database Performance Analyzer (DPA), which we do not believe is affected.</p><p class="mb-3">We encourage all customers to run only supported versions of our products and to upgrade to the latest versions to the get the full benefit of our updates, improvements and enhancements.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What products are NOT affected by the SUNBURST vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 36</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/20/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What products are NOT affected by the SUNBURST vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Our investigations are still ongoing, but based on our investigations to date, we have found no evidence that other versions of our Orion Platform products or any of our other products, Orion agents, or Web Performance Monitor (WPM) Players are affected by the SUNBURST vulnerability.
<br/></p><p class="mb-3">SolarWinds products <strong>NOT KNOWN TO BE AFFECTED</strong> by this security vulnerability are as follows:</p><table class="mb-7 w-full text-s-paragraph Manager</p><p class="mb-0">Storage Profiler</p><p class="mb-0">Threat Monitor</p><p class="mb-0">Virtualization Profiler</p><p class="mb-0">Web Help Desk</p><p class="mb-0">SQL Sentry</p><p class="mb-0">SentryOne Monitor</p><p class="mb-0">BI xPress</p><p class="mb-0"> </p><p class="mb-0"><strong>SolarWinds MSP Products:</strong></p><p class="mb-0">N-central – Probe</p><p gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Why didn’t SolarWinds catch the SUNBURST vulnerability before it happened?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 37</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Why didn’t SolarWinds catch the SUNBURST vulnerability before it happened?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">This SUNBURST vulnerability was very complex and sophisticated. It was crafted to evade detection and only run when detection was unlikely.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">With these processes in place how was your code compromised to insert the SUNBURST vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 38</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>With these processes in place how was your code compromised to insert the SUNBURST vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">We are not aware that the SolarWinds code base was compromised. Our initial investigations point to an issue in the Orion software build system in which the SUNBURST vulnerability was inserted which, if present and activated, could potentially allow an attacker to compromise the server on which the Orion Platform products run.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">How many customers are potentially affected by SUNBURST vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 39</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>How many customers are potentially affected by SUNBURST vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">We’ve currently identified less than 18,000 customers potentially affected by this security vulnerability.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Why were 33,000 customers mentioned in connection with the SUNBURST vulnerability?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 40</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 12/15/2020</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>Why were 33,000 customers mentioned in connection with the SUNBURST vulnerability?</strong></p><p class="mb-3">Out of an abundance of caution, we’ve communicated with all SolarWinds customers on active maintenance from February 2020 through current. We initially communicated with more customers than we believe were affected by the SUNBURST vulnerability, and this number was included in our <a href="https://investors.solarwinds.com/financials/sec-filings/sec-filings-details/default.aspx?FilingId=14559445" data-linktype="Glossary Rail" data-linkdetail="Form 8-K embed" data-automation-id="financials-sec-filings-sec-filings-details-default-aspx-link" class="break-words text-swdc-blue-500 underline hover:decoration-2 active:text-swdc-blue-600 active:decoration-2">Form 8-K</a> filed with the Securities Exchange Commission on December 14, 2020.</p></div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">What is the Common Criteria framework?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 41</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 2/4/2021</em></p><p class="mb-3"><strong>What is the Common Criteria framework?</strong></p>Common Criteria is a framework most often associated with federal organizations. It’s an international standard for computer security achieved by national laboratory testing and evaluation.</div></div><div class="flex gap-x-8"></div></div></div></div><div class="mt-5" style="scroll-margin-top:29px"><div><div class="flex flex-col"><h3 class="mb-3 text-2xl font-bold">Where can I see a complete list of Orion Suite for Federal Government versions, their status and recommended actions?</h3><div class="overflow-x-auto text-m-paragraph text-swdc-gray-400"><div><p class="mb-3"><strong>QUESTION 42</strong></p><p class="mb-3"><em>Recent as of 2/24/2021</em></p><p Based on our investigations to date, SUNBURST requires an internet connection to be activated and disconnecting your Orion server from the internet should immediately protect your environment from SUNBURST. The vulnerability in the product that allows for the deployment of SUPERNOVA, however, may still be exploited by a malicious actor who accesses your network from inside and not over the internet. Disconnecting from the internet will limit the ability of an external actor exploiting this vulnerability over an internet connection."}]},{"uid":"6733caa74e9b494eb43facbe56c1b196","type":"p","attrs":{},"children":[{"text":"IMPORTANT NOTE:","bold":true},{"text":" Disconnecting from the internet is not a recommended substitute for upgrading your Orion software to versions 2019.4.2, 2020.2.4, or 2020.2.5, or applying appropriate patches to older versions if a full upgrade is not possible at this time."}]}]},"orange_links":[],"orange_link":{"title":"","href":""},"orange_link_dlt":"","orange_link_dld":""},{"headline":"How is SolarWinds addressing SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA?","_metadata":{"uid":"cs5c8a9d32a7ecb481"},"nav_title":"","headline_element":"h3","hide_headline":false,"dlt":"Glossary Rail","dld":"How is SolarWinds addressing SUNBURST and SUPERNOVA?
